	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2016–17 Premier League</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

title="2017–18 Premier League">2017–18</a> → </div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>2016–17 Premier League</b> was the 25th season of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, the top English professional league for <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> clubs, since its establishment in 1992. The season began on 13 August 2016 and concluded on 21 May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Fixtures for the 2016–17 season were announced on 15 June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> won their fifth Premier League title, and sixth English title, with two matches to spare following a 1–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on 12 May.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The defending champions were <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, who finished 12th, thereby setting a new record for the worst Premier League title defence; the record had previously been held by Chelsea, who had finished 10th in <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16</a> after winning the title in <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">2014–15</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> entered as the three promoted teams from the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Football_League_Championship" title="2015–16 Football League Championship">2015–16 Football League Championship</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Premier_League_rebranding">Premier League rebranding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Premier League rebranding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 9 February 2016, the Premier League announced a rebrand; beginning with the 2016–17 season, the competition was known simply as the Premier League, without any sponsor's name attached. As part of the rebranding, a new logo was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticket_prices">Ticket prices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ticket prices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the beginning of the 2016–17 season, ticket prices for away fans were capped at £30 per ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Conte" title="Antonio Conte">Antonio Conte</a> enjoyed a successful start as Chelsea manager, winning the title in his first season at the club and earning a record number of league victories for a season, with only poor early form preventing them from also setting a new points total. Tottenham Hotspur shrugged off a disappointing Champions League campaign to push Chelsea close for the title, though they ultimately missed out. However, they finished the season with statistically both the best attack and defence, with striker <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kane" title="Harry Kane">Harry Kane</a> once again claiming the Golden Boot. Manchester City finished one spot better than the previous season in <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a>'s first season in charge, though ended the season trophy-less, despite recording the third-best attack and reaching the semi-finals of the FA Cup. Liverpool made the Champions League for the first time in three years in <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="Jürgen Klopp">Jürgen Klopp</a>'s first full season, though they were prevented from finishing any higher than fourth by an inconsistent start to 2017, a consequence of both losing their £35&#160;million signing <a href="/wiki/Sadio_Man%C3%A9" title="Sadio Mané">Sadio Mané</a> to international duty in January and February as well as suffering from several dropped points against bottom-half teams.
</p><p>Despite winning seven of their final eight games, Arsenal finished fifth and failed to qualify for the Champions League for the first time since 1997, as fan pressure on both manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> and majority-shareholder <a href="/wiki/Stan_Kroenke" title="Stan Kroenke">Stan Kroenke</a> grew. While they did win the FA Cup for the third time in four seasons, making Wenger the most successful manager in the competition's history, they endured yet another disastrous Champions League run, eliminated at the round of 16 for a seventh successive year. Manchester United finished sixth, one lower than the previous season, in <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>'s first season in charge, with their failure to turn any one of their 15 draws – with 12 earned amidst the season-record 25 matches unbeaten run – into victories proving problematic. They did at least win the EFL Cup and won the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2017 UEFA Europa League Final">Europa League final</a>. The latter was the first Europa League title in their history, not only securing a place in the Champions League but also made them only the fifth club to <a href="/wiki/UEFA_club_competition_records_and_statistics#List_of_teams_to_have_won_the_three_main_European_club_competitions" title="UEFA club competition records and statistics">have won all three major European trophies</a>.
</p><p>In only their second-ever top-flight season, AFC Bournemouth built on the success of the previous season as they secured a ninth-place finish and scored 55 goals, defying the critics who had tipped them to struggle from second-season syndrome. Much as Chelsea had the previous season, Leicester City made a poor defence of their title, despite having what turned out to be the best Champions League run of any English club this season. They were beaten by Hull City in the first match, the first time this has happened to a reigning Premier League champion. With the club struggling, manager <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a> was sacked in February and replaced by coach <a href="/wiki/Craig_Shakespeare" title="Craig Shakespeare">Craig Shakespeare</a>, who steered the club to 12th. It broke the record of the lowest finish for Premier League title holders, previously set by Chelsea, but comfortably clear of relegation.
</p><p>Swansea City had looked dead and buried after early struggles under <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Guidolin" title="Francesco Guidolin">Francesco Guidolin</a> and then a disastrous spell with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bradley" title="Bob Bradley">Bob Bradley</a> as manager, but were saved by a late improvement under <a href="/wiki/Paul_Clement_(football_manager)" title="Paul Clement (football manager)">Paul Clement</a>'s management. Burnley fared the best of the promoted clubs, with only atrocious away form preventing them finishing higher as they made their home-ground of Turf Moor one of the hardest places to get a point from – and secured a second successive top-flight season for the first time in 40 years. Watford, in their first successive top-flight campaign for 30 years, successfully ensured a third consecutive Premier League season – however, as a result of poor away form, a disastrous end to the season and several spells of indifferent form throughout the campaign, the Hornets were unable to really build on the previous season despite recording their first league victories over Manchester United and at Arsenal since the 1980s.
</p><p>After several successive escapes from relegation, Sunderland's resilience finally broke and they dropped into the Championship after a decade, having spent virtually the entire season rooted to the bottom of the table. Middlesbrough also struggled through their first top-flight season in eight years, with a poor end to the season, the weakest goal-scoring record in the division and an inability to turn one of their 13 draws into victories dooming them. Hull City were the final relegated side, never quite recovering from a disastrous pre-season which saw manager <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bruce" title="Steve Bruce">Steve Bruce</a> quit and next to no new players signed. Despite encouraging early season form under <a href="/wiki/Mike_Phelan" title="Mike Phelan">Mike Phelan</a>, a dismal run in the winter saw him sacked and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Marco_Silva" title="Marco Silva">Marco Silva</a>, who steered the club to a much better second half of the season, but it ultimately proved to be a case of too little, too late.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Twenty teams competed in the league&#160;– the top seventeen teams from the previous season and the three teams promoted from the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Football_League_Championship" title="2015–16 Football League Championship">Championship</a>. The promoted teams were <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>. Burnley and Hull City returned to the top flight after a season's absence while Middlesbrough returned after a seven-year absence. They replaced <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> (after a six-year top flight spell), <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> (relegated after a season's presence) and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> (after twenty-four years in the Premier League and twenty-eight years in the top flight).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums_and_locations">Stadiums and locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Stadiums and locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Stoke City announced that from the 2016–17 season onward the Britannia Stadium would be renamed to the Bet365 Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tottenham Hotspur played at White Hart Lane with a reduced capacity, due to the north east corner of the stadium being dismantled to help facilitate building works for their <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Development_Project" title="Northumberland Development Project">new stadium</a> being built adjacently.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">West Ham United played for the first time at the London Stadium, formerly known as the Olympic Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although having a capacity of 60,010, for the first Premier League game this was limited to 57,000 due to safety fears following persistent standing by fans at West Ham's Europa League game played in early August.<sup id="cite_ref-57k_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57k-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<div class="reflist">Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.premierleague.com/en-gb/matchday/league-table.html">Premier League</a><br />Rules for classification: 1) Points; 2) Goal difference; 3) Goals scored; 4) Play-offs (only if needed to decide champion, teams for relegation or teams for UEFA competitions).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><br /><span style="font-weight:bold">(C)</span> Champion; <span style="font-weight:bold">(R)</span> Relegated.<br />Notes:</div><div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-table_note_res_ELGS0.85404990280701-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-table_note_res_ELGS0.85404990280701_104-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Europa_League#Group_stage" title="2017–18 UEFA Europa League">Europa League group stage</a> by winning the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_FA_Cup" title="2016–17 FA Cup">2016–17 FA Cup</a>. As they had also qualified there by the virtue of their league position (5th), this spot was passed to the next-highest ranked team (6th), <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-table_note_res_ELTH0.85404990280701-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-table_note_res_ELTH0.85404990280701_105-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League#Group_stage" title="2017–18 UEFA Champions League">Champions League group stage</a> by winning the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2016–17 UEFA Europa League">2016–17 UEFA Europa League</a>. Based on their league position (6th), they would have received the spot above to enter the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Europa_League#Group_stage" title="2017–18 UEFA Europa League">Europa League group stage</a>. This spot was vacated without replacement as per UEFA regulations.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-table_note_res_EL3Q0.85404990280701-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-table_note_res_EL3Q0.85404990280701_106-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, winners of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EFL_Cup" title="2016–17 EFL Cup">2016–17 EFL Cup</a>, initially attained a spot in the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Europa_League#Third_qualifying_round" title="2017–18 UEFA Europa League">Europa League third qualifying round</a>. That was passed to the next-highest ranked team in the league not already qualified for UEFA competitions (7th-placed <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>).</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_awards">Annual awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Annual awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="infobox" style="width:180px;">
